<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Medjugorje" title="Our Lady of Medjugorje">Shrine of Our Lady Queen of Peace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Me%C4%91ugorje" class="mw-redirect" title="Međugorje">Međugorje</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to an estimation of the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina will have the third highest tourism growth rate in the world between 1995 and 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Newfound_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newfound-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Bosnia-Herzegovina had 747,827 tourists an increase of 9% and 1,645,521 overnight stays which is a 9.4% increase from 2012. 58.6% of the tourists came from foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, when ranking the best cities in the world, <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a> placed <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">national capital</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and host of the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">1984 Winter Olympic Games</a>, as #43, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a> at #59, <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a> at #84, <a href="/wiki/Bled" title="Bled">Bled</a> at #90, <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> at #113, and <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a> at #135.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Tourism in Sarajevo is chiefly focused on historical, religious, and cultural aspects. In 2010, Lonely Planet's "Best In Travel" nominated it as one of the top ten cities to visit that year.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Sarajevo also won travel blog Foxnomad's "Best City to Visit" competition in 2012, beating more than one hundred other cities around the entire world.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Me%C4%91ugorje" class="mw-redirect" title="Međugorje">Međugorje</a> has become one of the most popular pilgrimage sites for Christians in the world and has turned into Europe's third most important religious place, where each year more than 1 million people visit.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> It has been estimated that 30 million pilgrims have come to Međugorje since the reputed apparitions began in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bosnia has also become an increasingly popular skiing and <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">Ecotourism</a> destination. Bosnia and Herzegovina remains one of the last undiscovered natural regions of the southern area of the Alps, with vast tracts of wild and untouched nature attracting adventurers and nature lovers. <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic magazine</a> named Bosnia and Herzegovina as the best mountain biking adventure destination for 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-test_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-143">[143]</a></sup> The central <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Bosnian Dinaric Alps</a> are favored by hikers and mountaineers, containing both Mediterranean and Alpine climates. <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">Whitewater rafting</a> is somewhat of a <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national pastime</a>, with three rivers, including the deepest <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">river canyon</a> in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Tara_River_Canyon" title="Tara River Canyon">Tara River Canyon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Newfound_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newfound-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most recently, <a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a> named Bosnia and Herzegovina the "9th Greatest Adventure in the World for 2013", adding that the country boasts "the cleanest water and air in Europe; the greatest untouched forests; and the most wildlife. The best way to experience is the three rivers trip, which purls through the best the Balkans have to offer."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_attractions">Tourist attractions</span></h4>
<p>Some of the tourist attractions in Bosnia and Herzegovina include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, the "Olympic City" or "European Jerusalem"; the scientific, cultural, tourist and commercial center of Bosnia and Herzegovina</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vratnik_(Sarajevo)" title="Vratnik (Sarajevo)">Vratnik</a> old town and <a href="/wiki/Bijela_Tabija" title="Bijela Tabija">Bijela Tabija</a> fortress in Sarajevo</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medjugorje" title="Medjugorje">Shrine of Our Lady of Međugorje</a>, with Annual Youth Festival; the site of a <a href="/wiki/Marian_apparition" title="Marian apparition">Marian apparition</a> and subsequent Catholic pilgrimage destination</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a>, the "City on Neretva" or "City of Sunshine"; the location of the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stari_most" class="mw-redirect" title="Stari most">Stari most</a> and old-town Mostar</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vi%C5%A1egrad" title="Višegrad">Višegrad</a>, location of the UNESCO World Heritage Site of the <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_Pa%C5%A1a_Sokolovi%C4%87_Bridge" title="Mehmed Paša Sokolović Bridge">Mehmed Paša Sokolović Bridge</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">Banja Luka</a>, the "Green City", with sights such as the Kastel fortress and <a href="/wiki/Ferhat_Pasha_Mosque" title="Ferhat Pasha Mosque">Ferhadija mosque</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biha%C4%87" title="Bihać">Bihać</a> and the waterfalls of the river <a href="/wiki/Una_(Sava)" title="Una (Sava)">Una</a> within Una National Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jajce" title="Jajce">Jajce</a>, city of the Bosnian kings and the place where the Federal People's Republic of Yugoslavia was founded, Pliva lakes and waterfall</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prijedor" title="Prijedor">Prijedor</a>, featuring its Old City Mosque, <a href="/wiki/Kozara_National_Park" title="Kozara National Park">Kozara National Park</a> and, at Mrakovica, Bosnia's largest World War II monument</li>
<li>The salt-lakes of <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">Tuzla</a>, birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Me%C5%A1a_Selimovi%C4%87" title="Meša Selimović">Meša Selimović</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Neretva</a> river and the <a href="/wiki/Rakitnica" title="Rakitnica">Rakitnica</a> river canyons in <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Upper Neretva</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Trebi%C5%BEat_(river)" title="Trebižat (river)">Trebižat</a> river and its waterfalls at Kravice and Kočuša</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Buna_(Neretva)" title="Buna (Neretva)">Buna</a> with its spring and historic town of <a href="/wiki/Vrelo_Bune" title="Vrelo Bune">Blagaj</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Tara_(Drina)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tara (Drina)">Lower Tara</a> river canyon, the deepest canyon in Europe</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sutjeska_National_Park" title="Sutjeska National Park">Sutjeska National Park</a>, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Old-growth_forest" title="Old-growth forest">ancient forest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Peru%C4%87ica" title="Perućica">Perućica</a> (one of the last two remaining primeval forests in Europe) and the Sutjeska river canyon</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Po%C4%8Ditelj_(%C4%8Capljina)" class="mw-redirect" title="Počitelj (Čapljina)">Počitelj</a> historical village</li>
<li>Mount <a href="/wiki/Bjela%C5%A1nica_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="Bjelašnica Mountain">Bjelašnica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jahorina" title="Jahorina">Jahorina</a>, sites used during <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">XIV Olympic Winter Games in 1984</a></li>
<li>The coastal city of <a href="/wiki/Neum" title="Neum">Neum</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Doboj" title="Doboj">Doboj</a> and its 13th-century fortress</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stolac_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Stolac Municipality">Stolac</a>, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Begovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Begovina">Begovina</a> neighborhood and <a href="/wiki/Radimlja" title="Radimlja">Radimlja</a> tombstones</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Visoko,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Visoko, Bosnia and Herzegovina">Visoko</a>, city of the Bosnian nobility and monarchy, historical capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bosnia" title="Kingdom of Bosnia">Kingdom of Bosnia</a> and the site of the alleged <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_pyramids" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnian pyramids">Bosnian pyramids</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Proko%C5%A1ko_Lake" title="Prokoško Lake">Prokoško Lake</a> in Fojnica</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Te%C5%A1anj" title="Tešanj">Tešanj</a>, one of Bosnia's <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" title="List of oldest continuously inhabited cities">oldest known cities</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bijeljina" title="Bijeljina">Bijeljina</a>, known for its agriculture and ethnic village Stanišić</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lukavac" title="Lukavac">Lukavac</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Modrac_Lake" title="Modrac Lake">Modrac Lake</a>, the largest artificial lake in Bosnia and Herzegovina</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Travnik" title="Travnik">Travnik</a>, the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andrić</a> and once the capital city of the <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_Eyalet" title="Bosnia Eyalet">Bosnia Eyalet</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jablanica,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Jablanica, Bosnia and Herzegovina">Jablanica</a>, Museum of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Neretva" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Neretva">Battle of Neretva</a> and Old bridge destroyed by Yugoslav army in <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ostro%C5%BEac_Castle" title="Ostrožac Castle">Ostrožac Castle</a>, a 16th-century castle built by the Ottoman Empire and later expanded by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gornji_Vakuf" class="mw-redirect" title="Gornji Vakuf">Gornji Vakuf</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Konjic" title="Konjic">Konjic</a>, featuring Tito's underground nuclear bunker<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="center">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Education in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Education in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sarajevo_University_building.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Sarajevo_University_building.JPG/220px-Sarajevo_University_building.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Sarajevo_University_building.JPG/330px-Sarajevo_University_building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Sarajevo_University_building.JPG/440px-Sarajevo_University_building.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sarajevo_University_building.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sarajevo" title="University of Sarajevo">University of Sarajevo</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Law_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarajevo Law School">Faculty of Law</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Higher education has a long and rich tradition in Bosnia and Herzegovina. The first bespoke higher-education institution was a school of <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> philosophy established by <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Husrev-beg" title="Gazi Husrev-beg">Gazi Husrev-beg</a> in 1531. Numerous other religious schools then followed. In 1887, under the Austro-Hungarian Empire, a <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a> law school began a five-year program.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> In the 1940s the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sarajevo" title="University of Sarajevo">University of Sarajevo</a> became the city's first secular higher education institute. In the 1950s post-bachelaurate graduate degrees became available.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Severely damaged during the war, it was recently rebuilt in partnership with more than 40 other universities. There are various other institutions of higher education, including: <a href="/wiki/University_%22D%C5%BEemal_Bijedi%C4%87%22_of_Mostar" class="mw-redirect" title="University &quot;Džemal Bijedić&quot; of Mostar">University "Džemal Bijedić" of Mostar</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Banja_Luka" title="University of Banja Luka">University of Banja Luka</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mostar" title="University of Mostar">University of Mostar</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_East_Sarajevo" title="University of East Sarajevo">University of East Sarajevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tuzla" title="University of Tuzla">University of Tuzla</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_University_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina">American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Academy of Sciences and Arts of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Academy of Sciences and Arts of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, which is held in high regard as one of the most prestigious creative arts academies in the region.</p>
<p>Also, Bosnia and Herzegovina is home to several private and international higher education institutions, some of which are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_School_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Sarajevo School of Science and Technology">Sarajevo School of Science and Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_University_of_Sarajevo" title="International University of Sarajevo">International University of Sarajevo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_University_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina">American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Graduate_School_of_Business" title="Sarajevo Graduate School of Business">Sarajevo Graduate School of Business</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Burch_University" title="International Burch University">International Burch University</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Primary schooling lasts for nine years. Secondary education is provided by general and technical secondary schools (typically <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasiums</a>) where studies typically last for four years. All forms of secondary schooling include an element of <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational training</a>. Pupils graduating from general secondary schools obtain the <a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">Matura</a> and can enroll in any tertiary educational institution or academy by passing a qualification examination prescribed by the governing body or institution. Students graduating technical subjects obtain a <a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">Diploma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Culture of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Culture of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Architecture of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Architecture of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<p>The architecture of Bosnia and Herzegovina is largely influenced by four major periods where political and social changes influenced the creation of distinct cultural and architectural habits of the population. Each period made its influence felt and contributed to a greater diversity of cultures and architectural language in this region.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Media of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Media of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_(BHRT)_building,_Sarajevo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg/250px-Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg" width="250" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg/375px-Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg/500px-Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4652" data-file-height="1634" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>Television, magazines, and newspapers in Bosnia and Herzegovina are all operated by both state-owned and for-profit corporations which depend on <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subscription" class="mw-redirect" title="Subscription">subscription</a>, and other sales-related revenues. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Constitution of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Constitution of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>.</p>
<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Country_in_transition" class="mw-redirect" title="Country in transition">country in transition</a> with a post-war legacy and a <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Politics of Bosnia and Herzegovina">complex domestic political structure</a> Bosnia and Herzegovina's media system is under transformation. In the early post-war period (1995–2005), media development was guided mainly by international donors and cooperation agencies, who invested to help reconstruct, diversify, democratize and professionalize media outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EJC_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EJC-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Post-war developments included the establishment of an independent Communication Regulatory Agency, the adoption of a Press Code, the establishment of the Press Council, the decriminalization of label and defamation, the introduction of a rather advanced Freedom of Access to Information Law, and the creation of a Public Service Broadcasting System from the formerly state-owned broadcaster. Yet, internationally backed positive developments have been often obstructed by domestic elites, and the professionalisation of media and journalists has proceeded only slowly. High levels of partisanship and linkages between the media and the political systems hinder the adherence to professional code of conducts.<sup id="cite_ref-EJC_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EJC-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Literature of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:220px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andric_Ivo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Andric_Ivo.jpg/218px-Andric_Ivo.jpg" width="218" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Andric_Ivo.jpg/327px-Andric_Ivo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Andric_Ivo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="362" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andric_Ivo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Travnik" title="Travnik">Travnik</a>-born writer <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andrić</a> won the 1961 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> for his novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bridge_on_the_Drina" title="The Bridge on the Drina">The Bridge on the Drina</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bosnia and Herzegovina has a rich literature, including the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel prize">Nobel prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andrić</a> and poets such as Croat <a href="/wiki/Antun_Branko_%C5%A0imi%C4%87" title="Antun Branko Šimić">Antun Branko Šimić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksa_%C5%A0anti%C4%87" title="Aleksa Šantić">Aleksa Šantić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Du%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Jovan Dučić">Jovan Dučić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mak_Dizdar" title="Mak Dizdar">Mak Dizdar</a>, writers such as <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Top%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Zlatko Topčić">Zlatko Topčić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Me%C5%A1a_Selimovi%C4%87" title="Meša Selimović">Meša Selimović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semezdin_Mehmedinovi%C4%87" title="Semezdin Mehmedinović">Semezdin Mehmedinović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miljenko_Jergovi%C4%87" title="Miljenko Jergović">Miljenko Jergović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isak_Samokovlija" title="Isak Samokovlija">Isak Samokovlija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safvet_beg_Ba%C5%A1agi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Safvet beg Bašagić">Safvet beg Bašagić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdulah_Sidran" title="Abdulah Sidran">Abdulah Sidran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_Ko%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Petar Kočić">Petar Kočić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Hemon" title="Aleksandar Hemon">Aleksandar Hemon</a>, and Nedžad Ibrišimović. The National Theater was founded 1919 in Sarajevo and its first director was the dramatist <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Nu%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Branislav Nušić">Branislav Nušić</a>. Magazines such as <i><a href="/wiki/Novi_Plamen" title="Novi Plamen">Novi Plamen</a></i> or <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sveske.ba/en">Sarajevske sveske</a></i> are some of the more prominent publications covering cultural and literary themes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Art of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Art of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg/230px-Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg/345px-Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg/460px-Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stećci from Radimlja, near <a href="/wiki/Stolac" title="Stolac">Stolac</a> (13th century)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The art of Bosnia and Herzegovina was always evolving and ranged from the original medieval tombstones called <a href="/wiki/Ste%C4%87ci" class="mw-redirect" title="Stećci">Stećci</a> to paintings in <a href="/wiki/House_of_Kotromani%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Kotromanić">Kotromanić</a> court. However, only with the arrival of Austro-Hungarians did the painting renaissance in Bosnia really begin to flourish. The first educated artists from European academies appeared with the beginning of the 20th century. Among those are: <a href="/wiki/Gabrijel_Jurki%C4%87" title="Gabrijel Jurkić">Gabrijel Jurkić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_%C5%A0ain" title="Petar Šain">Petar Šain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Roman Petrović">Roman Petrović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lazar_Drlja%C4%8Da" title="Lazar Drljača">Lazar Drljača</a>.</p>
<p>After World War II artists like <a href="/wiki/Mersad_Berber" title="Mersad Berber">Mersad Berber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safet_Zec" title="Safet Zec">Safet Zec</a> rose in popularity.</p>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Ars_Aevi" title="Ars Aevi">Ars Aevi</a>, a museum of contemporary art that includes works by renowned world artists was founded in Sarajevo.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Music of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Music of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_patriotic_songs" title="List of Bosnia and Herzegovina patriotic songs">List of Bosnia and Herzegovina patriotic songs</a></div>
<p>Typical Bosnian and Herzegovinian songs are <i>ganga, rera</i>, and the traditional Slavic music for the folk dances such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kolo_(dance)" title="Kolo (dance)">kolo</a></i> and from Ottoman era the most popular is <a href="/wiki/Sevdalinka" title="Sevdalinka">sevdalinka</a>. Pop and Rock music has a tradition here as well, with the more famous musicians including <a href="/wiki/Dino_Zoni%C4%87" title="Dino Zonić">Dino Zonić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goran_Bregovi%C4%87" title="Goran Bregović">Goran Bregović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davorin_Popovi%C4%87" title="Davorin Popović">Davorin Popović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kemal_Monteno" title="Kemal Monteno">Kemal Monteno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zdravko_%C4%8Coli%C4%87" title="Zdravko Čolić">Zdravko Čolić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvir_Lakovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Elvir Laković">Elvir Laković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edo_Maajka" title="Edo Maajka">Edo Maajka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hari_Mata_Hari" title="Hari Mata Hari">Hari Mata Hari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dino_Merlin" title="Dino Merlin">Dino Merlin</a>. Other composers such as <a href="/wiki/%C4%90or%C4%91e_Novkovi%C4%87" title="Đorđe Novković">Đorđe Novković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al%27_Dino" title="Al' Dino">Al' Dino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haris_D%C5%BEinovi%C4%87" title="Haris Džinović">Haris Džinović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kornelije_Kova%C4%8D" title="Kornelije Kovač">Kornelije Kovač</a>, and many pop and <a href="/wiki/Rock_bands" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock bands">rock bands</a>, for example, <a href="/wiki/Bijelo_dugme" class="mw-redirect" title="Bijelo dugme">Bijelo Dugme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crvena_Jabuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Crvena Jabuka">Crvena Jabuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Divlje_Jagode" class="mw-redirect" title="Divlje Jagode">Divlje Jagode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indexi" title="Indexi">Indexi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plavi_orkestar" title="Plavi orkestar">Plavi Orkestar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zabranjeno_Pu%C5%A1enje" title="Zabranjeno Pušenje">Zabranjeno Pušenje</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambasadori" title="Ambasadori">Ambasadori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubioza_kolektiv" title="Dubioza kolektiv">Dubioza kolektiv</a>, who were among the leading ones in the former Yugoslavia. Bosnia is home to the composer <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_%C5%A0esti%C4%87" title="Dušan Šestić">Dušan Šestić</a>, the creator of the current <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of Bosnia and Herzegovina and father of singer <a href="/wiki/Marija_%C5%A0esti%C4%87" title="Marija Šestić">Marija Šestić</a>, composer <a href="/wiki/Sa%C5%A1a_Lo%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Saša Lošić">Saša Lošić</a> and pianist <a href="/wiki/Sa%C5%A1a_Toperi%C4%87" title="Saša Toperić">Saša Toperić</a>. In the villages, especially in Herzegovina, Bosniaks, Serbs, and Croats play the ancient <i><a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">Gusle</a></i>. The gusle is used mainly to recite epic poems in a usually dramatic tone.</p>
<p>Probably the most distinctive and identifiably "Bosnian" of music, Sevdalinka is a kind of emotional, melancholic folk song that often describes sad subjects such as love and loss, the death of a dear person or heartbreak. Sevdalinkas were traditionally performed with a <a href="/wiki/Saz_(musical_instrument)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saz (musical instrument)">saz</a>, a Turkish string instrument, which was later replaced by the accordion. However the more modern arrangement, to the derision of some purists, is typically a vocalist accompanied by the accordion along with snare drums, upright bass, guitars, clarinets and violins.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema_and_theatre">Cinema and theatre</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bosnia-Herzegovina_films" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Bosnia-Herzegovina films">List of Bosnia-Herzegovina films</a></div>
<p>Sarajevo is internationally renowned for its eclectic and diverse selection of festivals. The <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Film_Festival" title="Sarajevo Film Festival">Sarajevo Film Festival</a> was established in 1995, during the Bosnian War and has become the premier and largest film festival in the Balkans and South-East Europe.</p>
<p>Bosnia has a rich cinematic and film heritage, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>; many Bosnian filmmakers have achieved international prominence and some have won international awards ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> to multiple <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Ors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bear" title="Golden Bear">Golden Bears</a>. Some notable Bosnian filmmakers, screenwriters and cinematographers are <a href="/wiki/Danis_Tanovi%C4%87" title="Danis Tanović">Danis Tanović</a> (known for the Academy Award– and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a>–winning 2001 film <i><a href="/wiki/No_Man%27s_Land_(2001_film)" title="No Man's Land (2001 film)">No Man's Land</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Jury_Grand_Prix" title="Jury Grand Prix">Silver Bear Grand Jury Prize</a>–winning 2016 film <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Sarajevo" title="Death in Sarajevo">Death in Sarajevo</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Vukoti%C4%87" title="Dušan Vukotić">Dušan Vukotić</a> (won an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Animated_Short_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Animated Short Film">Oscar for best animated short</a> film in 1961 for <i><a href="/wiki/Ersatz_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ersatz (film)">Surogat</a></i> ("Ersatz"), being the first foreigner to do so), <a href="/wiki/Emir_Kusturica" title="Emir Kusturica">Emir Kusturica</a> (won two <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> at Cannes), <a href="/wiki/Jasmila_%C5%BDbani%C4%87" title="Jasmila Žbanić">Jasmila Žbanić</a> (won Golden Bear), <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Top%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Zlatko Topčić">Zlatko Topčić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ademir_Kenovi%C4%87" title="Ademir Kenović">Ademir Kenović</a>, Dino Mustafić, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Filipovi%C4%87" title="Benjamin Filipović">Benjamin Filipović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jasmin_Dizdar" title="Jasmin Dizdar">Jasmin Dizdar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pjer_%C5%BDalica" title="Pjer Žalica">Pjer Žalica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sr%C4%91an_Vuleti%C4%87" title="Srđan Vuletić">Srđan Vuletić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aida_Begi%C4%87" title="Aida Begić">Aida Begić</a> etc.</p>

</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_cuisine" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina cuisine">Bosnia and Herzegovina cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:247px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG/245px-Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG" width="245" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG/368px-Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG/490px-Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bosnian meat platter</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg/215px-Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg" width="215" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg/323px-Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg/430px-Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mostar_-_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_-_Waitress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A waitress in the Old City of <a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a> wearing an old <a href="/wiki/Bosniak" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosniak">Bosniak</a> dress</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bosnian cuisine uses many spices, in moderate quantities. Most dishes are light, as they are cooked in lots of water; the sauces are fully natural, consisting of little more than the natural juices of the vegetables in the dish. Typical ingredients include tomatoes, potatoes, onions, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">peppers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumbers</a>, carrots, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mushroom" title="Mushroom">mushrooms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zucchini" title="Zucchini">zucchini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">dried beans</a>, fresh beans, <a href="/wiki/Plum" title="Plum">plums</a>, milk, <a href="/wiki/Paprika" title="Paprika">paprika</a> and cream called <a href="/wiki/Smetana_(dairy_product)" title="Smetana (dairy product)">Pavlaka</a>. Bosnian cuisine is balanced between <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern</a> influences. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Ottoman</a> administration for almost 500 years, Bosnian food is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_cuisine" title="Greek cuisine">Greek</a>, and other former <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean</a> cuisines. However, because of years of Austrian rule, there are many influences from Central Europe. Typical meat dishes include primarily beef and <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a>. Some local specialties are <a href="/wiki/%C4%86evap%C4%8Di%C4%87i" class="mw-redirect" title="Ćevapčići">ćevapi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burek" class="mw-redirect" title="Burek">burek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolma" title="Dolma">dolma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarma_(food)" title="Sarma (food)">sarma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilav" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilav">pilav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goulash" title="Goulash">goulash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajvar" title="Ajvar">ajvar</a> and a whole range of Eastern sweets. Ćevapi is a grilled dish of minced meat, a type of <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a>, popular in former Yugoslavia and considered a national dish in Bosnia and Herzegovina<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Local wines come from <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a> where the climate is suitable for growing grapes. Herzegovinian <i>loza</i> (similar to Italian <a href="/wiki/Grappa" title="Grappa">Grappa</a> but less sweet) is very popular. Plum (<i>rakija</i>) or apple (<i>jabukovača</i>) alcohol beverages are produced in the north. In the south, distilleries used to produce vast quantities of <a href="/wiki/Brandy" title="Brandy">brandy</a> and supply all of ex-Yugoslav alcohol factories (brandy is the base of most <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic drinks</a>).</p>
<dl>
<dt>Leisure activities</dt>
</dl>
<p>Coffeehouses, where <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnian coffee">Bosnian coffee</a> is served in <a href="/wiki/Cezve" title="Cezve">džezva</a> with <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Delight" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Delight">rahat lokum</a> and sugar cubes, proliferate <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> and every city in the country. Coffee drinking is a favorite Bosnian pastime and part of the culture. Bosnia and Herzegovina is the tenth country in the entire world by per capita coffee consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_at_the_Olympics" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina at the Olympics">Bosnia and Herzegovina at the Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Football in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Football in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:197px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg/195px-20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg" width="195" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg/293px-20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg/390px-20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1859" data-file-height="2793" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20150331_2219_AUT_BIH_2704.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a>, playing for the Bosnian national football team in the year 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg/215px-Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg" width="215" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg/323px-Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg/430px-Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium" title="Asim Ferhatović Hase Stadium">Asim Ferhatović Hase Stadium</a> in Sarajevo hosted the opening ceremony to the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">1984 Winter Olympics</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bosnia and Herzegovina has produced many athletes, both as a state in Yugoslavia and independently after 1992. The most important international <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sporting event</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="History of Bosnia and Herzegovina">history of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> was the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">14th Winter Olympics</a>, held in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> from 7 to 19 February 1984. The <a href="/wiki/RK_Borac_Banja_Luka" title="RK Borac Banja Luka">Borac</a> <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a> club has won seven <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Handball_Championship" title="Yugoslav Handball Championship">Yugoslav Handball Championships</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/EHF_Champions_League" title="EHF Champions League">European Championship Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_European_Cup_(handball)" title="1975–76 European Cup (handball)">1976</a> and the <a href="/wiki/EHF_Cup" title="EHF Cup">International Handball Federation Cup</a> in 1991.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amel_Meki%C4%87" title="Amel Mekić">Amel Mekić</a>, Bosnian judoka, became <a href="/wiki/2011_European_Judo_Championships" title="2011 European Judo Championships">European champion</a> in 2011. Track and field athlete <a href="/wiki/Amel_Tuka" title="Amel Tuka">Amel Tuka</a> won the bronze medal in <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_800_metres" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics – Men's 800 metres">800 metres</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics">2015 World Championships</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamza_Ali%C4%87" title="Hamza Alić">Hamza Alić</a> won the silver medal in <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Athletics_Indoor_Championships_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_shot_put" title="2013 European Athletics Indoor Championships – Men's shot put">shot put</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Athletics_Indoor_Championships" title="2013 European Athletics Indoor Championships">2013 European Indoor Championships</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/KK_Bosna" class="mw-redirect" title="KK Bosna">Bosna</a> basketball club from Sarajevo were <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">European Champions</a> in <a href="/wiki/1978%E2%80%9379_FIBA_European_Champions_Cup" title="1978–79 FIBA European Champions Cup">1979</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_basketball_team" title="Yugoslavia national basketball team">Yugoslav national basketball team</a>, which won medals in every world championship from 1963 through 1990, included Bosnian players such as <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Hall_of_Fame" title="FIBA Hall of Fame">FIBA Hall of Famers</a> <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Dalipagi%C4%87" title="Dražen Dalipagić">Dražen Dalipagić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Deliba%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Mirza Delibašić">Mirza Delibašić</a>. Bosnia and Herzegovina regularly qualifies for the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">European Championship in Basketball</a>, with players including <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Teletovi%C4%87" title="Mirza Teletović">Mirza Teletović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nihad_%C4%90edovi%C4%87" title="Nihad Đedović">Nihad Đedović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jusuf_Nurki%C4%87" title="Jusuf Nurkić">Jusuf Nurkić</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_men%27s_national_under-16_and_under-17_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina men's national under-16 and under-17 basketball team">Bosnia and Herzegovina national u-16 team</a> won two gold medals in 2015, winning both <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2015_European_Youth_Summer_Olympic_Festival" title="Basketball at the 2015 European Youth Summer Olympic Festival">2015 European Youth Summer Olympic Festival</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/2015_FIBA_Europe_Under-16_Championship" title="2015 FIBA Europe Under-16 Championship">2015 FIBA Europe Under-16 Championship</a>.</p>
<p>Women's basketball club <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDKK_Jedinstvo_Tuzla" title="ŽKK Jedinstvo Tuzla">Jedinstvo Aida</a> from Tuzla won <a href="/wiki/EuroLeague_Women" title="EuroLeague Women">Women's European Club Championship</a> in 1989 and <a href="/wiki/Ronchetti_Cup" title="Ronchetti Cup">Ronchetti Cup</a> final in 1990, led by <a href="/wiki/Razija_Mujanovi%C4%87" title="Razija Mujanović">Razija Mujanović</a>, three times best female European basketball player, and <a href="/wiki/Mara_Laki%C4%87" title="Mara Lakić">Mara Lakić</a>.</p>
<p>The Bosnian <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> team was <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Chess_Championship" title="Yugoslav Chess Championship">Champion of Yugoslavia</a> seven times, in addition to club <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0K_Bosna" title="ŠK Bosna">ŠK Bosna</a> winning four <a href="/wiki/European_Chess_Club_Cup" title="European Chess Club Cup">European Chess Club Cups</a>. Chess grandmaster <a href="/wiki/Borki_Predojevi%C4%87" title="Borki Predojević">Borki Predojević</a> has also won two European Championships. The most impressive success of Bosnian Chess was runner-up position in <a href="/wiki/31st_Chess_Olympiad" title="31st Chess Olympiad">Chess Olympiad</a> of 1994 in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, featuring Grandmasters <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Predrag Nikolić">Predrag Nikolić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sokolov_(chess_player)" title="Ivan Sokolov (chess player)">Ivan Sokolov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bojan_Kurajica" title="Bojan Kurajica">Bojan Kurajica</a>.</p>
<p>Middle-weight <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxer</a> <a href="/wiki/Marijan_Bene%C5%A1" title="Marijan Beneš">Marijan Beneš</a> has won several Championships of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Yugoslav Championships and the European Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-nezavisne_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nezavisne-157">[157]</a></sup> In 1978, he won the World Title against <a href="/wiki/Elisha_Obed" title="Elisha Obed">Elisha Obed</a> from the Bahamas.</p>
<p>Association football is the most popular sport in Bosnia and Herzegovina. It dates from 1903, but its popularity grew significantly after World War I. Bosnian clubs <a href="/wiki/FK_Sarajevo" title="FK Sarajevo">FK Sarajevo</a> and <a href="/wiki/FK_%C5%BDeljezni%C4%8Dar_Sarajevo" title="FK Željezničar Sarajevo">Željezničar</a>, won the Yugoslav Championship, while the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslav national football team</a> included Bosnian players of all ethnic backgrounds and generations, such as <a href="/wiki/Safet_Su%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Safet Sušić">Safet Sušić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Vujovi%C4%87" title="Zlatko Vujović">Zlatko Vujović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_Ba%C5%BEdarevi%C4%87" title="Mehmed Baždarević">Mehmed Baždarević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davor_Jozi%C4%87" title="Davor Jozić">Davor Jozić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faruk_Had%C5%BEibegi%C4%87" title="Faruk Hadžibegić">Faruk Hadžibegić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Pa%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Predrag Pašić">Predrag Pašić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bla%C5%BE_Sli%C5%A1kovi%C4%87" title="Blaž Slišković">Blaž Slišković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vahid_Halilhod%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Vahid Halilhodžić">Vahid Halilhodžić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Bajevi%C4%87" title="Dušan Bajević">Dušan Bajević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivica_Osim" title="Ivica Osim">Ivica Osim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Katalinski" title="Josip Katalinski">Josip Katalinski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Knez" title="Tomislav Knez">Tomislav Knez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velimir_Sombolac" title="Velimir Sombolac">Velimir Sombolac</a> and numerous others. The <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team</a> played at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, its first major tournament. Notable players on the team included <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asmir_Begovi%C4%87" title="Asmir Begović">Asmir Begović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emir_Spahi%C4%87" title="Emir Spahić">Emir Spahić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miralem_Pjani%C4%87" title="Miralem Pjanić">Miralem Pjanić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhamed_Be%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Muhamed Bešić">Muhamed Bešić</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vedad_Ibi%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Vedad Ibišević">Vedad Ibišević</a>.</p>
<p>Former Bosnian footballers include <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Salihamid%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Hasan Salihamidžić">Hasan Salihamidžić</a>, who became only the second Bosnian to ever win a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> trophy, after <a href="/wiki/Elvir_Balji%C4%87" title="Elvir Baljić">Elvir Baljić</a>. He made 234 appearances and scored 31 goals for German club <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sergej_Barbarez" title="Sergej Barbarez">Sergej Barbarez</a>, who played for several clubs in the German <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> including <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayer_Leverkusen" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayer Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> was joint-top scorer in the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Bundesliga" title="2000–01 Bundesliga">2000–01 Bundesliga</a> season with 22 goals. <a href="/wiki/Meho_Kodro" title="Meho Kodro">Meho Kodro</a> spent most of his career playing in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> most notably with <a href="/wiki/Real_Sociedad" title="Real Sociedad">Real Sociedad</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>. <a href="/wiki/Elvir_Rahimi%C4%87" title="Elvir Rahimić">Elvir Rahimić</a> made 302 appearances for Russian club <a href="/wiki/CSKA_Moscow" title="CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> with whom he won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2005 UEFA Cup Final">2005</a>. <a href="/wiki/Milena_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Milena Nikolić">Milena Nikolić</a>, member of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina women's national football team">women's national team</a>, was <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Women's Champions League">2013–14 UEFA Women's Champions League</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League#Top_scorers" title="UEFA Women's Champions League">top scorer</a>.</p>
<p>Bosnia and Herzegovina was the world champion of <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_2004_Summer_Paralympics" title="Volleyball at the 2004 Summer Paralympics">volleyball at the 2004 Summer Paralympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="Volleyball at the 2012 Summer Paralympics">volleyball at the 2012 Summer Paralympics</a>. Many among those on the team lost their legs in the Bosnian War.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> is also gaining a lot of popularity after the recent successes of <a href="/wiki/Damir_D%C5%BEumhur" title="Damir Džumhur">Damir Džumhur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Ba%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Mirza Bašić">Mirza Bašić</a> at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> level. Other notable tennis players who represented Bosnia are, <a href="/wiki/Amer_Deli%C4%87" title="Amer Delić">Amer Delić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mervana_Jugi%C4%87-Salki%C4%87" title="Mervana Jugić-Salkić">Mervana Jugić-Salkić</a>.</p>

<li><sup>2</sup> Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.</li>
</ul>
